<div id="review_1175208062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1175208062" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1175208062?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476740324" href="/book/show/17571742-ten-tiny-breaths">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1175208062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8574972364038299823">How to start... How to start... Ok so <i>Ten Tiny Breaths</i> follows the story of Kacey Cleary, a girl who is trying to get her life back on track after a traumatic accident. Shortly after which, her and her sister move to live with her aunt and uncle. After that fails they decided to run away and move to Florida. I was drawn too this story for two reasons... The cover and the ratings. Almost everyone I'm friends with on GRs gave it 4 stars or higher... Which I'm kind of confused about.<br/><br/>The characters </span>
  <span id="freeText8574972364038299823" style="display:none">How to start... How to start... Ok so <i>Ten Tiny Breaths</i> follows the story of Kacey Cleary, a girl who is trying to get her life back on track after a traumatic accident. Shortly after which, her and her sister move to live with her aunt and uncle. After that fails they decided to run away and move to Florida. I was drawn too this story for two reasons... The cover and the ratings. Almost everyone I'm friends with on GRs gave it 4 stars or higher... Which I'm kind of confused about.<br><br>The characters in this book are just above okay. That's it though, just okay. Kacey is our leading lady. From the start I didn't like her. I get she has this hard outer shell because of what happened to her, but her attitude was 90% of the time just too much. If anyone said hi to her she wanted to fight them. She automatically assumed every guy wanted to sleep with her. We get that you're a fiery red head and all but calm your tits. Just because a guy says good morning doesn't mean he wants to jump your bones. Seriously, she spends pages and pages talking about punching people in the face... WE GET IT YOU TOOK A FEW KICK BOXING CLASSES!!! Towards the middle of the story I started to like her a lot more, but by the end I was hating her again. The whole <i>"don't hold my hand" </i>thing<i> </i>was so pointless. It seemed like it was going to be important, but was dropped so early on.<br><br><div>
<br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-57gr2absA8I/VNbPCHB8imI/AAAAAAAABMA/kLi8jkY7OfY/s1600/hand%2Bholding%2Bthing.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423365136ra/13612794.gif" height="169" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>
</div><br><br>Livie, Kacey's sister, just barely formed as a sub character. At first when the story started from the way Kacey talked to her, to the way the author portrayed her, I assumed both girls were a lot younger. I thought Livie was idk 8, and Kacey 17. Turns out ones 15 and ones 20. (<i>So that was awkward to discover.</i>) Livie was <b>BEYOND </b>annoyingly naive. Then there's Storm and her daughter Mia. This is going to sound harsh since Mia's all little and cute but still could careless for her character. Storm was the only lady in this book I actually liked. She was the perfect blend of sassy and sarcastic.<br><br>As far as males go there's only one you really need to know about, and that's Trent. Oh Trent where to start with you... <i>Should I start with your sexy dimples? Should I start with your six pack abs? No, I think I'll start with the fact that your character was <b>SO, SO predictable</b></i>! That and the fact that all he has to do is smile at Kacey and her Vagina bust out her pants. I'm all for girls getting weak in the knees over a guy but this chick took it to the next level. She can barley walk the whole novel. Something serious happens between the two characters toward mid-end and all ya boy has to do is say <i>"whoops my B" </i>and Kacey is back in love with him. I wont say what it is, but trust me it would take more than a couple of lopsided dimple smiles to make me forgive him. I just didn't like his character. I wont lie I like guys that are moody bad boys. Trent tries to wear a wolf mask but turns out he was just a sheep. I don't want my guys just showing up thinking looking hot is enough... I want some kind of emotion from them, even if it's just because they have some crazy in their eyes. I JUST WANT SOMETHING!!! Trent is the character that makes Kacey start "returning to her old self" but I have no idea what was it about Trent which made her decide to let her guard down? He does nothing but stalk. <i>(yeah I've found stalking hot in other tales, but not this one.) </i> <br>On top of all that this boy turned out to be some kind of super natural <br>human... He can literately make a girl climax by just looking at them. Yeah couldn't make that part up if I tried. <br><br>As far as the plot went, it went slow. I kept waiting and waiting for something to happen that would make my jaw drop, and it sadly never came. I figured out pretty early on what the "big reveal" was going to be. I was hoping there was going to be more to it and there wasn't. If someone didn't see it coming than I would naturally assume they had never read another ya/na novel before. The plot basically rinse, lather, repeats itself over and over again. The plot builds about as much as the story does... So yeah not at all. <b>THE ONLY, ONLY</b> thing I liked about this book was the meaning, and the way the phrase "Ten tiny breaths" was revealed.<br><br><i>&lt;“Just breathe. Ten tiny breaths. Seize them. Feel them. Love them...”</i><br>The meaning behind it was <b>BEAUTIFUL</b>! And I applaud Tucker for giving us such a wonderful quote with a powerful meaning to back it up. But even that sweet little nugget couldn't save this story for me. Everything down to the ending of this book just didn't reach me. I found myself having to do the tiny breath routine just to get to the ending. I wish this book would have lived up it all the hype and constant recommendations I was getting on it. Sadly, to me, it was just boring.<br><br><br><div>
<br><a href="http://1.bp.blogspot.com/-XzVQPcDdHjE/VNbRDSd277I/AAAAAAAABMM/olMFAztsgXc/s1600/boring.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423365136ra/13612795.gif" height="176" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>
</div><br><br><br></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_472149361" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/472149361" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/472149361?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781476740331" href="/book/show/17278200-ten-tiny-breaths">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=tough-subjects">tough-subjects</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=arc-or-galley">arc-or-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer472149361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7967102858356944199"><b>Initial reaction:</b> I think most people know from my status updates on this that I didn't like this book, but I think reflecting upon the work on a number of different levels, it's more than just one element or the measure that this fell into many New Adult cliches. This book really got under my skin on how poorly it was written, how poorly it treats some very weighted, but very real issues (PTSD, depression, etc.) and how it manipulates dramatic scenarios to the point that none of it felt real. T</span>
  <span id="freeText7967102858356944199" style="display:none"><b>Initial reaction:</b> I think most people know from my status updates on this that I didn't like this book, but I think reflecting upon the work on a number of different levels, it's more than just one element or the measure that this fell into many New Adult cliches. This book really got under my skin on how poorly it was written, how poorly it treats some very weighted, but very real issues (PTSD, depression, etc.) and how it manipulates dramatic scenarios to the point that none of it felt real. There is a part of me that's interested in hearing Liviey's story, because that's contained in the sequel, but honestly? I don't think the writing will carry that well based on what I see in this book. It may be subject to change/improve, but I honestly have no idea. This just wasn't done well. I have many bases to cover in the full review, but I'll try to be as concise about it as I can, and note some of my respective issues with it.<br /><br /><b>Full review:</b><br /><br />I sat on my hands intentionally before writing a review on "Ten Tiny Breaths" because I felt I needed to think about what didn't work with this book. Let alone the fact that the book upset and disappointed me on a number of different levels. I could go into an extended discussion on how there's really nothing new that distinguishes "Ten Tiny Breaths" from other titles in the "coined" New Adult genre, but for me, this actually could've been a much better novel if the writing wasn't so terrible among other aspects. It makes many basic mistakes on the level of the narrative aspects of the writing as well as the presentation of many different issues. And it's emotionally manipulative to top it off.<br /><br />Some of you might be wincing at this point and say "Rose, that's harsh" but when I say emotionally manipulative here, I don't say it with much snark or mirth. I'm saying that the story - in technical terming - manipulates the emotional resonance in a horrible way here. Whether it was intentional or unintentional, I don't know, but I really think this story could've been so much stronger than what it was - I saw where it was going, I saw what it was trying to do. It just didn't handle it well at all; I've read stories in other terms that have taken these issue and made them hit home with so much more impact. Further, there were a number of things in this story that really offended me. I'll address much of that shortly.<br /><br />Let's begin by talking about Kacey, the protagonist. She's a tough cookie for sure considering she's suffering from a heavy measure of PTSD after a horrific accident in which her family, boyfriend, and pretty much everyone she loved was killed except for her and her little sister Livie, who happened to stay home that day. Kacey was the only survivor of the crash. I would expect her to be bitter, go through the motions, and be psychologically damaged. I would expect her to lash out and have trouble with relationships and have recollections from the crash, alongside nightmares that perhaps her family (Poor, poor Livie) would have to contend with from time to time. Those factors I didn't mind at all. I also didn't mind the fact that she ran off with her little sister (15-year old Livie, who was pretty much the major character I liked somewhat consistently in this book, even if she wasn't always at the forefront). Livie was nearly molested by their uncle, and that prompted Kacey to pick up their things and get away from home. I actually didn't like how the book depicted them leaving home - what with some drug induced manipulations and whatnot, but I figured for the sake of the story, I'd follow it.<br /><br />Kacey really turned out to be a horrible protagonist in more ways than one, basically coming across in spurts as the female version of Travis Maddox from Beautiful Disaster. She slut shames every woman she comes across (including her neighbor Storm, who I have to say was a nice character in framework and I would've liked to see more of her than Kacey). Kacey uses and loses people she sleeps with, thinks every man she comes across is a misogynistic twat (which to be honest, every single male character in this really <i>is</i> misogynistic in some way, including the hero). Kacey has a penchant for violence and she either thinks of beating down the people she's around or she actually does so in physical measures (I'm trying to figure out how the author thought this was okay?). There's also another confrontation where she came close to killing a man with a broken bottle. I'm not going to say she didn't have her reasons because of events, but I still couldn't wrap my head around her actions even in context with what occurred.<br /><br />On the level of the writing in this, it was very tedious to move through - Kacey does a lot of info-dumping and repeating of the accidents events in bits and pieces up to the actual recall, which makes the narrative overbearing and overselling/stating the point. In a more mature narrative, it probably wouldn't have been a problem, but the writing is juvenile the way it's presented. Melodramatic even. Cliched, certainly, to the level of committing several offenses. I could talk about the slut shaming, body shaming, bitch slamming, sexual objectification, misogyny among other things that goes along with other NA reads in current spectra, but I want to turn attention briefly to another problematic issue that rears its head in this novel: racial appropriation.<br /><br />Yeah, I'm going there. Pretty much the only two minority characters featured in this book are sexually objectified and/or shamed in some way. They're both strippers, and while their occurrence may fit somehow in the context of where Kacey works, I didn't get any other impression in this novel other than they were there as diversity set pieces. The Asian stripper was shamed because of a certain way she could move her body (and that had the underlying subtext of denouncing her), while a Native American stripper is shamed in a manner by doing a version of a "rain dance" when she's nearly naked.<br /><br />I'm going to be blunt with saying this - characters of color are NOT an author's personal set pieces to be moved around willy nilly. You can't just throw them into a scene and make stereotypical assumptions/statements and think "Oh hey, I'm being diverse!". Because like the assumption of portraying a Native American with stereotypical feathers and doing some sort of dance in a strip club when that "dance" has significant symbolic value to a tribe (who isn't even really named, it's just following stereotype), you use it in the wrong way. You shame the group, you offend the group, and it's a HORRIBLE way to portray any person or group. Authors, don't do this. Please. When portraying any group of color, think about how you're portraying them. Seriously, please THINK. <br /><br />Moving on with the story dynamic, Kacey, as the protagonist, overfixates her attention on her love interest Trent, who when her "walls" aren't being broken down just by being in his presence, she spends long passages talking about his physical features - the specks in his eyes, his physical body and "looking him up and down" (when she isn't being looked up and down herself). I'm not saying that physical objectification doesn't exist in other narratives, but it came to a point I wanted to say that the author was doing it TOO much to the point where I just felt ill at ease with it and noted the repetition. Kacey somehow pours all of her trust into being with this guy even when she doesn't know much about him, and shames any woman who comes close to him.<br /><br />On that note, let's talk about Trent. Or maybe I shouldn't, because when this novel was all said and done, I wanted to say "Screw Trent" with the power of a thousand...somethings. Trent is emotionally manipulative in his own way - I cannot with people who use sexual encounters as emotional leverage to get the other person they love to do things. Kacey is obviously a damaged person. He recognizes this, tells her to get help even when she's resistant against him. Kacey does call him out on the fact of witholding sexual encounters to make her admit things she doesn't want to admit (and yet she does them anyway). Yet he's just as reluctant to talk about his own past (then again Kacey doesn't ask). <br /><br />When a certain twist in the narrative comes to the forefront that involves his and Kacey's relationship, I thought that could've been used as a conflict of worthiness if it was done right (even if I didn't like some of the implications behind it). Yet, the events after said twist were so creepy and unrealistic that I wanted to throw my computer against the wall. It was manipulative, championing, deceitful and made this one of the worst narratives I've read this year for its subject matter. I do not understand why stalkerish relationships in the NA genre are somehow championed and made to be romantic. This book is especially creepy considering the knowledge Trent has before this point and what he did with those measures, and it's equally unrealistic to think that with the emotional turmoil that Kacey has been through before and after these events (which I would say is so overblown with drama that I felt my head rushing with blood), that everything would turn out to be just fine.<br /><br />In a line from a Maroon 5 song, and I run the risk of being slightly cheese with saying this: "It's not always rainbows and butterflies, it's compromise that moves us along." That actually could've went along with this particular narrative's thematic, but the story felt so contrived and didn't deal with any of the issues realistically for the exceedingly heavy emotional weights presented here. It was pure melodrama and played right along with the cliche that "love conquers/heals all."<br /><br />I'm sorry to be the bummer of the party, but that's not true. Not the reality for who suffers from PTSD/depression. It can take a long time for someone like Kacey to heal IRL, and there could've been so many more constructive, fuller ways for her to come to terms with what happened. Hinging her recovery on Trent and who he reveals himself to be after the twist plays into a horrible mentality that Kacey can't heal herself unless it's by loving someone or having someone heal her, rather than healing herself. The twist and the revelations behind that twist didn't make that any better with what she emotionally goes through. I felt sick with some of the apologetic bargaining that Kacey's therapist forced her through. The only time I think I actually felt for Kacey's coming to terms was when her sister Livie pretty much told her to buck up and that she was tired of going through the same things that her older sister put her through. I wanted to hug Livie after that because she was spot on. I just wish that there were more of that actual, genuine resonance in this story than there was.<br /><br />I cannot recommend this book to anyone, because for a narrative on PTSD/depression, finding love, and showing the developing relationship of two people in difficult circumstances here was VERY mediocre, melodramatic B.S., and perpetuates so many stereotypes in the NA genre that I couldn't even begin to wrap my head around. There are SO MANY novels that deal with this theme better and it's just a matter of looking. This was very weak in comparison, and champions a lot of problematic ideals for the sake of drama.<br /><br />Overall score: 0.5/5<br /><br />Note: I received this as an ARC from NetGalley, from the publisher Atria.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7967102858356944199" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1297607425?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476740324" href="/book/show/17571742-ten-tiny-breaths">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=2015-reads">2015-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=sobfest">sobfest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=highly-recommended-na">highly-recommended-na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=annoying-heroines">annoying-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=owned-physical-copy">owned-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=new-adult-contemporary">new-adult-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=hot-male-characters">hot-male-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1297607425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12225163586817628103"><b>I've just read another phenomenal book!</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443588458i/16382272.jpg' width='250' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I picked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15990969.Ten_Tiny_Breaths__Ten_Tiny_Breaths___1_' title='Ten Tiny Breaths (Ten Tiny Breaths, #1) by K.A. Tucker' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ten Tiny Breaths</a> because of its postive reviews on Goodreads and I'm so happy that I made a great decision. It did not disappoint. The story was handled and delivered well by the author.<br/><br/><b>Ten Tiny Breaths</b> tells us a story about the main character <b>Kacey Cleary</b> whose life has changed ever since the day her parents, her boyfriend, and her bestfriend died in a car accident. It's the accident where she was the only one who survived. When she and her siste</span>
  <span id="freeText12225163586817628103" style="display:none"><b>I've just read another phenomenal book!</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443588458i/16382272.jpg" width="250" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I picked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15990969.Ten_Tiny_Breaths__Ten_Tiny_Breaths___1_" title="Ten Tiny Breaths (Ten Tiny Breaths, #1) by K.A. Tucker" rel="nofollow noopener">Ten Tiny Breaths</a> because of its postive reviews on Goodreads and I'm so happy that I made a great decision. It did not disappoint. The story was handled and delivered well by the author.<br><br><b>Ten Tiny Breaths</b> tells us a story about the main character <b>Kacey Cleary</b> whose life has changed ever since the day her parents, her boyfriend, and her bestfriend died in a car accident. It's the accident where she was the only one who survived. When she and her sister <b>Livie </b> moved to Miami to start a new life, she met the tall, gorgeous, and intriguing guy <b>Trent Emerson</b> whom she had an immediate attraction to. She later on became attached to him-- but with reluctance, because of her issues.<br><br>I am a fan of romance books with deep and heavy drama behind, and I must say that this book really brought out the emotions in me. Although <b>the writing style of the author didn't feel as captivating to me at first</b>, I enjoyed the book as I've read further because of the surprisingly peculiar effect it had in me.<br><br><b>Kacey</b> is a great character. She's a headstrong woman. What I like about her is the way she became determined to protect her sister from anyone who became a threat to them. I wish I have a sister like her! I have to admit that at first, I really had a hard time liking her. She's one of those whiny female leads that constantly annoy me, but then I quickly warmed up to her the moment the author presented the details about her traumatic past. I ended up a bit feeling awed by her.<br><br><b>Trent</b> is also one amazing character that is worthy to be praised. I love how he was introduced in a mysterious manner. I also love his gentleness towards Kacey and the way he became a remarkable part of the book.<br><br><i>
  <b>"Just breathe. Ten tiny breaths … Seize them. Feel them. Love them."</b>
</i><br><br>The thing you can expect about <b>Ten Tiny Breaths</b> is the beautiful impact afterwards. It's a story about <b>love, grief, denial, healing, and forgiveness</b>. I appreciate how <b>moving on</b> was greatly emphasized here. I highly recommend!<br><br>(I've read this along with my sissy <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/36178759-queennicay" rel="nofollow noopener">QueenNicay</a>. Thank you, sis! xoxo)</span>

  <td colspan="2">

  <span id="freeText10780738538046569137" style="display:none"><b>“Just breathe...<br>Ten tiny breaths ...<br>Seize them...<br>Feel them...<br>Love them...”</b><br><br><br><i>Breath</i><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404929i/788306.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><i>How many deaths can you bear before you get drowned?</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/480300.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Will you ever recover from your past?</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404929i/788307.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Kacey</b><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404929i/788308._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Kacey lost her parents , her best friend and her boyfriend in a car accident.Since then she was living at her aunt's house .<br>After an incident Kacey decided that it wasn't safe for her and her sister to live there and they ran away.<br>They moved to a new town.<br>They started a new life.<br><br><b>"Our pasts isnt who we are.I'm me and you are you and that's who we need to be."</b><br><br>There they met Storm and her five year old daughter Mia.<br>Livvie and Mia started to spend a lot of time together and Kacey after all these years she found someone who she could rely on.<br><br><b>Trent</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379789477i/523075._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He was her hot neighbor.He wanted to be with her from the first moment but whenever he got a chance he wouldn't grab it.<br>He wanted things between them to be real.<br><br><b>“I want to make you smile. Let me make you smile.”</b><br><br>Kacey is trapped in her past and her only escape is kicking sand bags until her knuckles are red.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380404929i/788309._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In the first half of the book she is cold and full of hate for those bastards who took the lives'of her most beloved people.<br>Her only wish is:<u>vengeance</u><br><br><b>"Hatred is good.Forgiveness is bad."</b><br><br>However, meeting Trent changed her life.<br><br><b>"Trent held my hand and I didnt drown."</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380404929ra/788310.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>He made her happy..<br>He made her laugh..<br>He took her nightmares away..<br>He made her <b>feel again</b>.</i><br><br><b>“I'll make you whole again, Kacey. I promise you, I will.”<br><br>“Trent has kept his promise. He makes me smile every day.”</b><br><br>Trent had also secrets and when I read what he did I coulnd believe it.<br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380404929ra/788311.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Why I liked this book</u>: This book was setting a good example.<br>Vegeance is not the most important thing in our lives. <div id="review_408477682" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/408477682" />
    <a title="Lucia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8837962-lucia"><img alt="Lucia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484242793p2/8837962.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/408477682?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucia" href="/user/show/8837962-lucia">Lucia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16700492-ten-tiny-breaths">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8837962-lucia?shelf=bookshelves-owned">bookshelves-owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer408477682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3819289749789532097">My Kacey and Trent:<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390296i/751915.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"The blue floors, the rusty old machines, the walls, everything around me vanishes under the weight if his gaze as it strips me of my protective bitch coat, yanking it clean off my body, levaing me bare and vulnerable in second."</b>
</blockquote><br/>After tragical death of Kacey's dearest ones and after her younger sister was almost molested by their uncle, Kacey decides to act as Livie's guardian and run away with her to Miami to start over again. But after everything Kacey had to go through,</span>
  <span id="freeText3819289749789532097" style="display:none">My Kacey and Trent:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380390296i/751915.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>"The blue floors, the rusty old machines, the walls, everything around me vanishes under the weight if his gaze as it strips me of my protective bitch coat, yanking it clean off my body, levaing me bare and vulnerable in second."</b>
</blockquote><br>After tragical death of Kacey's dearest ones and after her younger sister was almost molested by their uncle, Kacey decides to act as Livie's guardian and run away with her to Miami to start over again. But after everything Kacey had to go through, she is different person, bitter, full of pain, almost like a living shell, keeping her distance from everyone. Until she meets her new neighbour, good looking and charming Trent, who knows exactly how to get through that protective wall of hers...<br><br>Ten Tiny Breaths is one of those stories that after reading blurb you think you know exactly what it is going to be about but once you start reading you do not have an idea what hit you. This book is perfect, unique and definitely one of the most interesting contemporary novels I have read this year. It was my first book by K. A. Tucker and I really liked the "voice" of this story and style of writing in general. <br><br>Ten Tiny Breaths is book about ways of dealing with death of close person and overcoming the trauma. Everyone deals with pain and sorrow differently. Some people need to open up, someone needs a time and some people think they are lost forever in their hatrage and bitchiness. The last mentioned is the case of 20 years old Kacey, the narrator of this book. Kacey was very interesting character, I could feel her pain and understood her decisions even though I did not always agree with her. <br><br>Ten Tiny Breaths is about Trent, main male character who got my full attention from the very fist moment he appeared in this story. He was charming, playful, nice and attractive in every possible way. BUT (there is always but right?) he had his own issues and secrets.<br><br>Ten Tiny Breaths is about <b>forgiveness</b> - about letting anger go and letting forgiveness to heal you when you feel broken.<br><br>Ten Tiny Breaths is about strong passion and desire between two young people who never expected to find happiness again.<br><br>Ten Tiny Breaths is about...life is short so just read this book yourself and find out. <b>It is so worth it!!!</b><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Just breathe," my mom would say. "Ten tiny breaths ... Seize them. Feel them. Love them."</i>
</blockquote><br>MORE REVIEWS ON MY BLOG <a href="http://readingismybreathing.blogspot.cz/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <b>Reading Is My Breathing</b>
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3819289749789532097" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1882421432" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1882421432" />
    <a title="Ramona Popescu " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33526516-ramona-popescu"><img alt="Ramona Popescu " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594649997p2/33526516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1882421432?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ramona Popescu " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ramona Popescu " href="/user/show/33526516-ramona-popescu">Ramona Popescu </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1882421432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7593006871710900863">I've heard to much about this series and I know that K.A.Tucker is a wonderful writer, that truly provides her readers with the most genuine and real stories. This depth I am talking about will surely connect with everybody because we all know life sometimes can be hard, but we must find a reason to keep going.<br/><br/>So, taking into consideration the above info, let me tell you something about the story. Kacey has been through a lot. After losing her parents, best friend and boyfriend in a terrible acc</span>
  <span id="freeText7593006871710900863" style="display:none">I've heard to much about this series and I know that K.A.Tucker is a wonderful writer, that truly provides her readers with the most genuine and real stories. This depth I am talking about will surely connect with everybody because we all know life sometimes can be hard, but we must find a reason to keep going.<br><br>So, taking into consideration the above info, let me tell you something about the story. Kacey has been through a lot. After losing her parents, best friend and boyfriend in a terrible accident, she is lost and literally hanging on for dear life. One day, in order to protects her sister, Olivia, from their uncle, she decides to leave her old life and move to Miami. They want to start fresh, leave behind the terrible events that marked them forever. Easily said than done. With no money, because their uncle made sure to lose them at playing cards, they have to start from scratch. <br><br>But how? Kacey didn't graduate, Olivia doesn't have the age to work and they have to make a living from something. With the little resources they have, they rent out an apartment and try to find a solution. Kacey feels so lost and not because she can't provide for herself, but she has to do something for her sister, because she is the only one in her life that means the world to her. Enter Trent Emerson, the guy next door. He moved in recently and he's as mysterious as it can be. Of course he is smart, gorgeous and extremely persistent. He instantly clicks with Kacey and sets up his goal to befriend her. Of course friendship will lead to other steamy and romantic things, but the readers have to be patient.<br><br>So, this is all about the plot. Why 5 stars?<br><br>First, the characters were amazingly built and here I am talking especially about Kacey. She is not your typical heroine. After the accident she changed dramatically. She became involved with drugs, fights and one night stands, using that rush and adrenaline to keep her emotions together. She didn't talk to anybody about that night and as time passed, she built up a wall that couldn't be destroyed easily. Violence and a hard exterior were her only defense mechanism and she used them permanently. Olivia was everything for her and she focused that energy in seeing her well provided, paying her studies and maybe one day seeing her happy. There was no time to think about herself, and despite a very traumatizing experience, she didn't received the proper treatment then, becoming " The after Kacey".<br><br>When meeting Trent she couldn't believe how instable she was around him, how her walls came crumbling down and how alive she felt around him. Trent at first sight is perfect, caring so much about Kacey and making her feel special, but there are a lot of things we don't know about him and as the plot progresses, be prepared to be surprised and why not, cry. I know I did:) <br><br>If you think this is a normal love story, you are in for a disappointment. A lot of connections will be made regarding our characters past and many secrets will be revealed that will completely turn their world upside down. This is a very different love story, born from hurt and suffering and I won't spoil much because there are some twist and turns that will leave you completely shattered, and they are key to our heroes relationship. What I can say is that their love will be tested and despite everything, everyone deserves a chance to be happy and whole again. This element of moving on was very important for the writer, because her focus was not only on Kacey's ability to do so, but also on Trent's past and issued that will connect with Kacey. Just wait and see. <br><br>And one last thing. This book raises awareness about PTSD symptoms and I believe it is so important to read carefully and try to connect with the characters and maybe learn something from it. There are so many people in the world that didn't ask for help when the time came, so if anybody knows a similar case, please don't hesitate in taking a stand and help them, until it's too late. With the proper medical help and love from friends and close ones, anybody can start over.<br><br>5 beautiful stars!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479123324i/21149668._SX540_.png" width="500" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For more reviews please check <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://readwithloveblog.wordpress.com">https://readwithloveblog.wordpress.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7593006871710900863" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1809436064" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1809436064" />
    <a title="Norma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41400192-norma"><img alt="Norma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589038160p2/41400192.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1809436064?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Norma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Norma" href="/user/show/41400192-norma">Norma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476740324" href="/book/show/17571742-ten-tiny-breaths">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1809436064" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8583524728296405088">This gets 4 **** bright stars from me!! TEN TINY BREATHS by K.A TUCKER is a New Adult novel that is beautifully written, emotional and ends up as a feel good read which I thought was quite good! To be honest I didn't even realize that there was even such a genre as New Adult, I had to google it! This was definitely a page turner and extremely hard to put down.<br/> <br/>I am following my new review format for this read as mostly all of my points of a complete reading experience do apply for this one. Usua</span>
  <span id="freeText8583524728296405088" style="display:none">This gets 4 **** bright stars from me!! TEN TINY BREATHS by K.A TUCKER is a New Adult novel that is beautifully written, emotional and ends up as a feel good read which I thought was quite good! To be honest I didn't even realize that there was even such a genre as New Adult, I had to google it! This was definitely a page turner and extremely hard to put down.<br /> <br />I am following my new review format for this read as mostly all of my points of a complete reading experience do apply for this one. Usually I go into a book blind so the synopsis of a book doesn't necessarily come into play in most of my reviews. That is why I usually don't do a summary of the plot.<br /> <br />THE COVER really grabbed my attention as it was appealing and after reading it I found that it was also very fitting. The cover really depicts that as the story is about a girl who finds herself drowning in the pain of her broken heart and how she overcomes that through the love of a boy who has his own dark secrets and who ultimately helps her to breath, to live, and to love again.<br /> <br />Favorite quote: "Give me your heart, Kasey. I'll take everything that comes with it."<br /> <br />THE TITLE was absolutely spot on for this one. TAKE TEN TINY BREATHS. SEIZE THEM. FEEL THEM. LOVE THEM.<br /> <br />TEN TINY BREATHS has us following along Kasey’s journey through the stages of her life after the accident. <br /> <br />Stage One - Comfortably Numb<br />Stage Two - Denial<br />Stage Three - Resistance<br />Stage Four - Acceptance<br />Stage Five - Dependence<br />Stage Six - Withdrawal<br />Stage Seven - Breakdown<br />Stage Eight - Recovery<br />Stage Nine - Forgiveness<br />Final Stage - Epilogue<br /> <br />I loved Kasey’s CHARACTER and her voice throughout this novel. She was damaged, strong, angry, vulnerable and could be also be a little violent at times. I also really enjoyed the authors writing style and how she delivered this story as she got you right into Kasey’s head and had you feeling her pain and her emotions as you followed along with Kasey's journey and all the different stages of her healing. I felt the love and chemistry between Kasey and Trent and the determination he had in trying to make her smile and to help her deal with her pain. I found TEN TINY BREATHS was easy to follow along with the storyline and all the secondary characters involved.<br /> <br />I don't normally read romance novels but this was definitely a nice change from all the Thrillers &amp; Suspense novels that I normally read. Although I did have some suspicion quite early on how one of the characters was going to be involved and when it actually is revealed I have to say my heart went out to this character. The ENDING was quite touching, satisfying and very pleasing for a very pleasant reading experience.<br /> <br />At the end of the book I fell in love with both Kacey &amp; Trent and all of my TEN TINY BREATHS taken throughout this novel. I will definitely be reading the rest of the novels in this series!<br /><br />To sum it all up it was a fast-paced, touching love story, that was a quick &amp; easy read with a very satisfying ending. Would recommend!!<br /><br />This review can also be found on Two Sisters Lost in a Coulee Reading book blog:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com/">https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8583524728296405088" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_476720983" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/476720983" />
    <a title="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog"><img alt="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1429608146p2/12994342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/476720983?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Smitten&#39;s Book Blog" href="/user/show/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog">Smitten&#39;s Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/16700492-ten-tiny-breaths">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=amazing-sexual-tension">amazing-sexual-tension</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=super-romantic-reads">super-romantic-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12994342-smitten-s-book-blog?shelf=emotional-reads">emotional-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer476720983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13661826268483221812"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400736i/776986._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400736i/776987._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>My Kacey and Trent<br/><br/>Fantastic book! I was in a huge book hangover from my last read and I was worried that whatever I read next would be difficult, but <i>Ten Tiny Breaths</i> was just what I needed.<br/><br/>It was a really easy read. I flew through it in about twelve hours and it was relatively pain free.<br/><br/>The characters were great. Trent was impossible not to fall in love with from the very beginning. He was sexy and seductive, with his panty dropping laundromat introductions... I was hooked.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I think I'm g</b></i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText13661826268483221812" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400736i/776986._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400736i/776987._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>My Kacey and Trent<br><br>Fantastic book! I was in a huge book hangover from my last read and I was worried that whatever I read next would be difficult, but <i>Ten Tiny Breaths</i> was just what I needed.<br><br>It was a really easy read. I flew through it in about twelve hours and it was relatively pain free.<br><br>The characters were great. Trent was impossible not to fall in love with from the very beginning. He was sexy and seductive, with his panty dropping laundromat introductions... I was hooked.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I think I'm going to fall in love with this man.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>As the book progressed, his sensitivity just pulled me further and further under his spell. He's a fantastic, gorgeous, adorable hero and I'm officially adding Trent Emerson to my ever growing collection of book boyfriends.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"I want to make you smile. For real. Always. We're going to go for dinners, and see movies, and walk on the beach. We'll go hang gliding, or bungee jumping or whatever you want to do. Whatever makes you smile and laugh more. Let me make you smile."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>*swoon*<br><br>Kacey was clearly tormented, but ballsy and quite comical at times. I like that she didn't resist for <i>too</i> long, to Trent's charms. After all, a book where the heroine spends the entire time rebuffing the hero is no fun for anyone.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>I crave his presence, his body, his voice, his laugh, his everything. <br>I need him. <br>I need Trent.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>There were some great surrounding characters that really made this book what it was... Storm, Livie, Mia, Ben, Nate, Cain, Officer Dan, Tanner... they were all great and played their small but fundamental parts. There were some great witty one liners.<br><br>The sexual chemistry in this book is palpable! I found myself fanning myself on numerous occasions as Trent and Kacey wound each other up to the boiling point. Completely scrummy! Oh how, love a good dose of sexual frustration!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>For two years, I haven't given anyone the time of day. Now, here I am, day one into our new life, and I'm ready to straddle this guy on the washer.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>But ultimately, this book is a moving story of forgiveness, coping through adversity and love. Love for family, love for friends and finding love in the most unlikely places. I shed a tear a couple of times and the beautiful ending made my heart swell! <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Hope. Hope that something beautiful may come from this tragic story.<br>Fear. Fear that it won't.<br>Forgiveness ... forgiveness.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400736i/776988._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>To read more reviews go to my Book Blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://smittensbookblog.wordpress.com/">http://smittensbookblog.wordpress.com/</a><br>Follow me on Twitter: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/SmittenSC">https://twitter.com/SmittenSC</a><br>Find me on Pinterest: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://pinterest.com/smittensc/">http://pinterest.com/smittensc/</a><br>Join in the chat on Facebook: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/groups/427743250626754/?fref=ts">http://www.facebook.com/groups/427743...</a></span>

<div id="review_470309114" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/470309114" />
    <a title="Jenny Levine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12673270-jenny-levine"><img alt="Jenny Levine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353067785p2/12673270.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/470309114?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenny Levine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenny Levine" href="/user/show/12673270-jenny-levine">Jenny Levine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12673270-jenny-levine?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer470309114" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4761233634197857121"><blockquote> <b> <i> “Just breathe,” <br/>“Ten tiny breaths… <br/>Seize them.<br/>Feel them.<br/>Love them.” </i> </b> </blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399780i/773995.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ten Tiny Breaths is about <b> Kacey Cleary </b> and the <b> <u> Stages of her Life </u> </b><br/><br/><b> <u> Stage One ~ <i> Comfortably Numb </i> </u> </b><br/>After a tragic drunk driving accident that took the lives of her parents, best friend, and boyfriend, Kacey became an Ice Queen.<br/><i> Before Kacey </i> was a sweet girl. Her irises shined when she laughed. She had tons of friends, and she snuck in hugs and kisses and handholding with her boyfriend whenever she could. But that <i> Ka</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4761233634197857121" style="display:none"><blockquote> <b> <i> “Just breathe,” <br>“Ten tiny breaths… <br>Seize them.<br>Feel them.<br>Love them.” </i> </b> </blockquote><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380399780i/773995.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ten Tiny Breaths is about <b> Kacey Cleary </b> and the <b> <u> Stages of her Life </u> </b><br><br><b> <u> Stage One ~ <i> Comfortably Numb </i> </u> </b><br>After a tragic drunk driving accident that took the lives of her parents, best friend, and boyfriend, Kacey became an Ice Queen.<br><i> Before Kacey </i> was a sweet girl. Her irises shined when she laughed. She had tons of friends, and she snuck in hugs and kisses and handholding with her boyfriend whenever she could. But that <i> Kacey </i> is gone.<br><i> After Kacey? </i> Well, she's a mess. She sunk into the world of sex, drugs and alcohol as her coping mechanism. She doesn't cry. She doesn’t open up about anything; she can’t stand the feel of hands because they remind her of death. She doesn’t let people in. Kickboxing is her way of forgetting the pain caused by her past.<br><br><i> I’m not Kacey Cleary anymore.<br>I’m an empty shell who cracks inappropriate jokes and feels nothing.<br>I’m a Kacey imposter. </i><br><br>After the death of her parents, together with her sister <b> Livie </b> (who is an angel, btw), they lived with their Aunt Darla and Uncle Raymond. But because of their uncle's little "visit" to Livie's room, Kacey decided it's time for them to leave. They came across an apartment in Miami, wherein she will meet new friends, and the guy who will change her life...<b> Trent. </b><br><br><b> <u> Stage Two ~ <i> Denial </i> </u> </b><br><b> Trent Emerson. </b> Gorgeous hottie (with dimples!) neighbor. Their meeting was uneventful. Why? Because when Kacey saw Trent, she became speechless. She felt something different about him, and developed instant attraction. And then she met her other neighbor, <b> Storm </b>. She's blonde, hot, a real-life barbie. NUH UH. Don't judge the book by it's cover. She's <u> NOT </u> A BITCH. She's a genuine friend, and she also has a daughter, which Livie is very fond of. And of course, Kacey, being Kacey, shut them down and denied access to her life.<br><br><b> <u> Stage Three ~ <i> Resistance </i> </u> </b><br>Thanks to Storm, Kacey's now working at the bar (or Strip Club) where Storm is working. They're not strippers, ok. They're bartenders. One night, she spotted Trent. And no, he's not watching the naked pretzel on the stage. He's actually watching her.<br><br>One day, when she was in the shower at her apartment, a rather funny "incident" happened, and Trent saved her...NAKED. She can't deny her attraction to him and so <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ she kissed him. and he kissed her.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. After that, Trent became a regular at the bar, always watching her, and Kacey starts flirting with him too. When the unimaginable happened:<br><br><i> So slow, so light, my fingertip skims his index finger. He still doesn’t move his hand. He remains completely frozen, as if waiting for me to make my move. Swallowing hard, I let my entire hand skate over his. I hear a sharp intake of air as he gasps, his jaw clenching. His eyes are locked on mine and they’re unreadable. Finally, his hand shifts and covers mine, his fingers gently slipping in between. Not forceful, not rushed.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/432854.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I can’t contain the euphoria swelling inside me. Trent’s touch is full of life. </i><br><br>Then, Trent asked her: <i> "Is this okay?" </i><br><br><b> <u> Stage Four ~ <i> Acceptance </i> </u> <br>YES. </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399780ra/773996.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She answered <u> YES </u> to the handholding. Or maybe even more?<br>Because after that, things became better for her.<br><br><i> “I want to make you smile. For real. Always. We’re going to go for dinners, and see movies, and walk on the beach. We’ll go hang-gliding, or bungee jumping, or whatever you want to do. Whatever makes you smile and laugh more.”<br><br>“Let me make you smile.” </i><br><br><b> <u> Stage Five ~ <i> Dependence </i> </u> </b><br>Days pass and on each day, she realizes how attached she is to Trent. When he isn't around she misses him. She <i> needs </i> Trent.<br><br>So again, another problem. Trent convinced her to join a Support Group, which she agrees to. But, she cannot take it. She isn't ready (or will she ever be ready?) to talk about her past and thinks he's hurting her. And said:<br><br><i> “Stay away from me.” I spin around and stalk down the sidewalk.<br>I don’t look back.<br>Trent doesn’t chase. </i><br><br><b> <u> Stage Six ~ <i> Withdrawal </i> </u> </b><br><b> Trent's gone. </b> Will he come back? You have to find out what happens next.<br><br>I'll leave you with that, and the few stages of Kacey's life. Stages 7-9 ~ <b> <i> Breakdown. Recovery. Forgiveness. </i> </b> Because I think those are the most important parts of the story and I don't want to spoil it all for you :)<br><br><b> <u> THOUGHTS: </u> </b><br>I LOVED IT. I love the cover. The prologue and epilogue is perfect. Ten Tiny Breaths is AMAZING.<br>I loved all the characters in this story. They are all likable especially Kacey's sister, Livie. She's just so selfless and she's a positive person. She's mature for her age, maybe more mature than her sister, to be honest. She has one of the most beautiful lines said in this book --&gt; <i> "Our past isn’t who we are. I’m me and you’re you and that’s who we need to be." </i> I hope Kacey learns from her. And I want a sister like her :)<br>And of course, Trent. My new book boyfriend. He's a breath of fresh air ;)<br>I love K.A. Tucker's style of writing, plus the humor and the emotions she put in the book.<br>There's a twist in the story (which I totally figured out). IDK, man, I think it's that obvious, but I still enjoyed it and there are times I cried. I also find some of the scenes repetitive and Kacey, the heroine, can be annoying at times. Nevertheless, it's a great read!<br><br>Overall, I enjoyed reading this. This book teaches us not to dwell on the past, move on...and most importantly, learn to FORGIVE.<br><br><b> HIGHLY RECOMMENDED! </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380399780ra/773997.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=why-u-no-longer-u-make-me-sad">why-u-no-longer-u-make-me-sad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=favorite-couple">favorite-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=cut-my-heart-out">cut-my-heart-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=they-are-so-cute-its-unbearable">they-are-so-cute-its-unbearable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=be-my-heroes-please">be-my-heroes-please</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=friends-love-like-it">friends-love-like-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=contains-unlovable-heroines">contains-unlovable-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5705623-kristalia?shelf=it-s-so-hot-in-here">it-s-so-hot-in-here</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer552177907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16108735270800635258"><b>Final rating: 4.75/5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i> <b>“I want to make you smile. For real. Always. We’re going to go for dinners, and see movies, and walk on the beach. We’ll go hang-gliding, or bungee jumping, or whatever you want to do. Whatever makes you smile and laugh more.” His fingers toy with my bottom lip. “Let me make you smile.” </b></i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Wow. Wow. Wow. At first, i wasn't impressed with this book. I didn't connect with the main character - in fact, she pissed me off. I didn't find the story interesting, felt that it </span>
  <span id="freeText16108735270800635258" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 4.75/5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i> <b>“I want to make you smile. For real. Always. We’re going to go for dinners, and see movies, and walk on the beach. We’ll go hang-gliding, or bungee jumping, or whatever you want to do. Whatever makes you smile and laugh more.” His fingers toy with my bottom lip. “Let me make you smile.” </b></i>
</blockquote><br><br>Wow. Wow. Wow. At first, i wasn't impressed with this book. I didn't connect with the main character - in fact, she pissed me off. I didn't find the story interesting, felt that it needed more, and wondered if it was going to continue being like it whole book. <b>But then, the last 40% were mind blowing. I must admit - in the end i <i> was </i> impressed. </b> Not to mention that i cried. I CRIED, while i thought it wouldn't make me :P  <br><br><blockquote>
  <i> <b>“You hate me, don’t you? You must hate me. I can’t help it. I’m broken.”<br>Trent squeezes me close to him. “I don’t hate you. I could never hate you. Give me your heart, Kacey. I’ll take everything that comes with it.”</b></i>
</blockquote><br><br><b> First half of the book left me wondering - Why? Why did i start this book? Do i even like it? Do i like the Kacey? Do i like the story?</b> <br><br><u>The answers i had in the end were like this: </u><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>Why? Why did i start this book?</i>
</b><br><br>-Because all of my friends loved it and i believe them. <br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>Do i even like it?</i>
</b><br><br>-In the end, i did. I really did. It was heart breaking afterall. I didn't expect that kind of a plot twist, but it broke me down. And it broke Kacey down. <br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>Do i like the Kacey?</i>
</b><br><br>-At first, she pissed me off. She was way to stubborn, she was annoying, she hurt people intentionally with words. But that is the way she coped. She lost her family, boyfriend and best friend in one night. And all that she had left was her sister. In the end, she changed, she forgave, she felt again. And i slowly connected to her again. <br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>Do i like the story? </i>
</b><br><br>-Yes, yes, ten thousand times, YES! At first, it was just normal story - boy meets girl type. But the last 40% of it proved me wrong. It wasn't an ordinary story and it deserves attention, love and to be read.<br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>Characters</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Kacey:</u>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Like i said before, i didn't like Kacey for the first half of the book. She was selfish, she hurt people, she destroyed herself. She thought that she was imposter. Kacey's imposter. After the incident, she was never the same. She doesn't want to <i> feel </i> anything. She is broken, inside and out. Or so she thought until she was made to feel again by Trent. She lets him in her life, slowly...but it pains her. Deeply. It broke her down into pieces, only to heal slowly, patiently, in time.<br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Trent:</u>
  </i>
</b> <br><br>I fell in love with him. He is a wonder. I loved him, despite everything that had happened. He is amazing, bright, funny, wonderful. Almost perfect. Except that he isn't perfect - he hides something, he hides his past. Just like Kacey does. He begins to fall in love in Kacey, her each move, each smile, her craziness. <br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Livie:</u>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Livie was wonderful character. She was always there, holding Kacey whole, her only support, not allowing her shatter in pieces. She is funny, cute and adorable. I can't wait to find more about her in the next book.<br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Storm &amp; Mia:</u>
  </i>
</b> <br><br>Storm and her daughter Mia were amazing characters. Storm is funny, crazy, works in a stripper club, falls in love eventually and is great friend and support to the two girls. I liked her so much :)<br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Others:</u>
  </i>
</b> <br><br>there were so many characters in this book who are amazing. Ben, Dan, everyone!<br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>SERIOUS SPOILER SECTION, DON'T SAY LATER I DIDN'T WARN YOU</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I still can't believe who Trent actually is. His real name, given name, is Cole. The same Cole who gave his keys to his best friend, the same guy who then found out that he had lost everything - that his decision killed 6 people. He tries to cope with it, but he couldn't, after all, it's not easy. Until he got the idea of stalking Kacey for 2 years. He wanted to connect with her, so she could forgive him - for all he had done. She was his coping mechanism, if she didn't forgive him, he would probably go crazy or insane. I understand him, i really do. And i am glad that in the end, Kacey forgave him. He suffered so much, and he deserved to be happy, just as much as she did.<br> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>OVERALL</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br><b> Truly a beautiful book. I was left speechless in the end, and i don't regret reading this one. If you have guts to survive 50% of the book, then i highly recommend it :D </b><br><br><b>
  <i>This review can be found on my blog: <a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">infinity-of-time.blogspot.com</a> also known as... </i>
</b><br><a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/2013/05/ten-tiny-breaths-ten-tiny-breaths-1-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363317i/714576.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/471169081?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Kyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Kyle" href="/user/show/9916227-jennifer-kyle">Jennifer Kyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9916227-jennifer-kyle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9916227-jennifer-kyle?shelf=cry-baby-books">cry-baby-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer471169081" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14855958094057629358"><b>
  <i>”Ten tiny breaths...Seize them. Feel them. Love them.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><span>[image error]</span><br/><br/>In an attempt not to swoon all over this review (I LOVED everything about this book!!!) or give anything away, I'll try to keep it simple. <br/><br/>This story takes you on a journey to Miami with Kacey and her sister, Livie. We take each step with Kacey as she slowly walks through her grief and numbness to living and feeling.<br/><br/><b>
  <i>”I’m not Kacey Cleary anymore. I’m an empty shell who cracks inappropriate jokes and feels nothing. I’m a Ka</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText14855958094057629358" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>”Ten tiny breaths...Seize them. Feel them. Love them.”</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>In an attempt not to swoon all over this review (I LOVED everything about this book!!!) or give anything away, I'll try to keep it simple. <br><br>This story takes you on a journey to Miami with Kacey and her sister, Livie. We take each step with Kacey as she slowly walks through her grief and numbness to living and feeling.<br><br><b>
  <i>”I’m not Kacey Cleary anymore. I’m an empty shell who cracks inappropriate jokes and feels nothing. I’m a Kacey imposter.”</i>
</b>~ Kacey<br><br>I adored each and every character and their role in Kacey’s journey- Storm, Princess Mia, Officer Dan, Ben, Cain, Nate, Tanner and last but SO not least…Trent. <br><br><b>
  <i>”Isn’t it exhausting?” The pad of his thumb strokes my neck softly.<br>“What?”<br>“Keeping people out.”</i>
</b>~ Trent<br><br><b>
  <i>”How can he see what I don’t want him to see, what I work so hard to conceal? He’s found a way in, that’s how. Like a trespasser, he’s invaded my space, breaching security and sliding in to take what I haven’t offered him.”</i>
</b>~ Kacey<br><br>Trent’s feelings for Kacey on his quest for her love and smiles had me swoony!<br><br><b>
  <i>"I want to make you smile. For real. Always. We're going to go for dinners, and see movies, and walk on the beach. We'll go hang-gliding, or bungee jumping, or whatever you want to do. Whatever makes you smile and laugh more." His fingers toy with my bottom lip. "Let me make you smile."</i>
</b>~Trent<br><br><b>
  <i>"You hate me, don't you? You must hate me. I can't help it. I'm broken." Trent squeezes me close to him. "I don't hate you. I could never hate you. Give me your heart, Kacey. I'll take everything that comes with it."</i>
</b>~Trent<br><br>This is a story about love, loss, healing, forgiveness and rebirth. It presents the reader the sad truth that in most tragedies there are two sides which are forever affected and healing can’t be completed without forgiveness.<br><br>Thank you K.A. Tucker for this story! This is a definite reread story for me. I’ve already went back numerous times to reread my favorite parts that bring both tears and smiles! <br><br><br><br></span>
